<p><b>Chad</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/En-us-Chad.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; padding: 0 .1em;" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Chad.ogg" title="File:En-us-Chad.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/tʃ/ 'ch' in 'china'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">tʃ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">æ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'d' in 'dye'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">d</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar"><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>تشاد</b></span></span>‎ <i><span title="DIN 31635 Arabic" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">Tšād</span></i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>Tchad</i></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Chad</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> to the southwest and <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> to the west. It is the fifth largest country in Africa in terms of area.</p>
<p>Chad is divided into multiple regions: a <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> zone in the north, an arid <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a> belt in the centre and a more fertile <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> zone in the south. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>, after which the country is named, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetland</a> in Chad and the second-largest in Africa. <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena" title="N'Djamena">N'Djamena</a>, the capital, is the largest city. Chad is home to over 200 different <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_in_Chad" title="List of ethnic groups in Chad">ethnic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Chad" title="Languages of Chad">linguistic groups</a>. <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> are the official languages. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> are the most widely practiced religions.</p>
<p>Beginning in the 7th millennium BC, human populations moved into the Chadian basin in great numbers. By the end of the 1st millennium BC, a series of states and empires rose and fell in Chad's Sahelian strip, each focused on controlling the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> routes that passed through the region. France conquered the territory by 1920 and incorporated it as part of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>. In 1960, Chad obtained independence under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Tombalbaye" title="François Tombalbaye">François Tombalbaye</a>. Resentment towards his policies in the Muslim north culminated in the eruption of a long-lasting <a href="/wiki/The_Tombalbaye_Regime#Rebellion_in_Chad" title="The Tombalbaye Regime" class="mw-redirect">civil war</a> in 1965. In 1979, <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_National_Unity" title="Transitional Government of National Unity">the rebels</a> conquered the capital and put an end to the south's hegemony. However, the rebel commanders fought amongst themselves until <a href="/wiki/Hiss%C3%A8ne_Habr%C3%A9" title="Hissène Habré">Hissène Habré</a> defeated his rivals. He was overthrown in 1990 by his general <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a>. Since 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict" class="mw-redirect">Darfur crisis</a> in Sudan has spilt over the border and <a href="/wiki/War_in_Chad_(2005%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Chad (2005–present)" class="mw-redirect">destabilised the nation</a>, with hundreds of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_refugees" title="Sudanese refugees" class="mw-redirect">Sudanese refugees</a> living in and around camps in eastern Chad.</p>
<p>While many political parties are active, power lies firmly in the hands of President Déby and his political party, the <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_Salvation_Movement" title="Patriotic Salvation Movement">Patriotic Salvation Movement</a>. Chad remains plagued by political violence and recurrent attempted <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coups d'état</a>. Chad is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">poorest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">most corrupt</a> countries in the world; most inhabitants live in poverty as <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Chad" title="Agriculture in Chad">subsistence herders and farmers</a>. Since 2003, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">crude oil</a> has become the country's primary source of export earnings, superseding the traditional <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> industry.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Chad" title="History of Chad">History of Chad</a></div>
<p>In the 7th millennium BC, ecological conditions in the northern half of Chadian territory favored human settlement, and the region experienced a strong population increase. Some of the most important <a href="/wiki/African_archaeology" title="African archaeology">African archaeological</a> sites are found in Chad, mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti_Region" title="Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region">Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region</a>; some date to earlier than 2000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For more than 2,000 years, the Chadian Basin has been inhabited by agricultural and <a href="/wiki/Sedentism" title="Sedentism">sedentary</a> people. The region became a crossroads of civilisations. The earliest of these were the legendary <a href="/wiki/Sao_civilisation" title="Sao civilisation">Sao</a>, known from artifacts and oral histories. The Sao fell to the <a href="/wiki/Kanem_Empire" title="Kanem Empire">Kanem Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lange88_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lange88-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> the first and longest-lasting of the empires that developed in Chad's <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a> strip by the end of the 1st millennium AD. The power of Kanem and its successors was based on control of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> routes that passed through the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> These states, at least tacitly <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Africa" title="Islam in Africa">Muslim</a>, never extended their control to the southern grasslands except to <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">raid for slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> In Kanem, about a third of the population were slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg/220px-Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg/330px-Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg/440px-Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="528" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Group of Kanem-Bu warriors. The <a href="/wiki/Kanem-Bornu_Empire" title="Kanem-Bornu Empire">Kanem-Bornu Empire</a> controlled almost all of what is today Chad.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg/220px-Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg/330px-Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg/440px-Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3286" data-file-height="2836" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Chadian soldier fighting for <a href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" title="Free French Forces" class="mw-redirect">Free France</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The Free French Forces included 15,000 soldiers from Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empires" title="French colonial empires" class="mw-redirect">French colonial expansion</a> led to the creation of the <span lang="fr"><i>Territoire Militaire des Pays et Protectorats du Tchad</i></span> in 1900. By 1920, France had secured full control of the colony and incorporated it as part of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Chad" title="Colonial Chad" class="mw-redirect">French rule in Chad</a> was characterised by an absence of policies to unify the territory and sluggish modernisation compared to other French colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-Decalo.2C_pp._8.E2.80.939_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decalo.2C_pp._8.E2.80.939-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The French primarily viewed the colony as an unimportant source of untrained labour and raw cotton; France introduced large-scale cotton production in 1929. The colonial administration in Chad was critically understaffed and had to rely on the dregs of the French civil service. Only the <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a> of the south was governed effectively; French presence in the Islamic north and east was nominal. The educational system suffered from this neglect.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Decalo.2C_pp._8.E2.80.939_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decalo.2C_pp._8.E2.80.939-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, France granted Chad the status of <a href="/wiki/Overseas_departments_and_territories_of_France" title="Overseas departments and territories of France">overseas territory</a> and its inhabitants the right to elect representatives to the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_France" title="National Assembly of France" class="mw-redirect">French National Assembly</a> and a <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Chad)" title="National Assembly (Chad)">Chadian assembly</a>. The largest political party was the <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Progressive_Party" title="Chadian Progressive Party">Chadian Progressive Party</a> (PPT), based in the southern half of the colony. Chad was granted independence on 11 August 1960 with the PPT's leader, a <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara people</a> <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Tombalbaye" title="François Tombalbaye">François Tombalbaye</a>, as its first <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state_of_Chad" title="Heads of state of Chad" class="mw-redirect">president</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Two years later, Tombalbaye banned opposition parties and established a one-party system. Tombalbaye's autocratic rule and insensitive mismanagement exacerbated interethnic tensions. In 1965 Muslims began a <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_National_Unity" title="Transitional Government of National Unity">civil war</a>. Tombalbaye was <a href="/wiki/Chadian_coup_of_1975" title="Chadian coup of 1975">overthrown and killed</a> in 1975,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> but the insurgency continued. In 1979 the rebel factions conquered the capital, and all central authority in the country collapsed. Armed factions, many from the north's rebellion, contended for power.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The disintegration of Chad caused the collapse of France's position in the country. <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> moved to fill the power vacuum and became <a href="/wiki/Chadian-Libyan_conflict" title="Chadian-Libyan conflict" class="mw-redirect">involved in Chad's civil war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Libya's adventure <a href="/wiki/Toyota_War" title="Toyota War">ended in disaster</a> in 1987; the French-supported president, <a href="/wiki/Hiss%C3%A8ne_Habr%C3%A9" title="Hissène Habré">Hissène Habré</a>, evoked a united response from Chadians of a kind never seen before<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> and forced the Libyan army off Chadian soil.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Habré consolidated his dictatorship through a power system that relied on corruption and violence with thousands of people estimated to have been killed under his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The president favoured his own <a href="/wiki/Daza" title="Daza" class="mw-redirect">Daza</a> ethnic group and discriminated against his former allies, the <a href="/wiki/Zaghawa_people" title="Zaghawa people">Zaghawa</a>. His general, <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a>, overthrew him in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Attempts to prosecute Habré led to his placement under house arrest in Senegal in 2005; in 2013, Habré was formally charged with war crimes committed during his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_(cropped)2014.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png/220px-Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png/330px-Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png 2x" data-file-width="405" data-file-height="439" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_(cropped)2014.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Despite internal political opposition, coup attempts and a civil war Idriss Deby has continuously ruled Chad since 1990</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Déby attempted to reconcile the rebel groups and reintroduced multiparty politics. Chadians approved a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Chad" title="Constitution of Chad">new constitution</a> by <a href="/wiki/Chadian_constitutional_referendum,_1996" title="Chadian constitutional referendum, 1996">referendum</a>, and in 1996, Déby easily won a <a href="/wiki/Chadian_presidential_election,_1996" title="Chadian presidential election, 1996">competitive presidential election</a>. He won a <a href="/wiki/Chadian_presidential_election,_2001" title="Chadian presidential election, 2001">second term</a> five years later.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> exploitation began in Chad in 2003, bringing with it hopes that Chad would at last have some chances of peace and prosperity. Instead, internal dissent worsened, and a <a href="/wiki/War_in_Chad_(2005%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Chad (2005–present)" class="mw-redirect">new civil war</a> broke out. Déby <a href="/wiki/Chadian_constitutional_referendum,_2005" title="Chadian constitutional referendum, 2005">unilaterally modified the constitution</a> to remove the two-term limit on the presidency; this caused an uproar among the civil society and opposition parties.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006 Déby won <a href="/wiki/Chadian_presidential_election,_2006" title="Chadian presidential election, 2006">a third mandate</a> in elections that the opposition boycotted. Ethnic violence in eastern Chad has increased; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> has warned that a <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> like that in <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict" class="mw-redirect">Darfur</a> may yet occur in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2006)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2006)">In 2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2008)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2008)">in 2008</a> rebel forces have attempted to take the capital by force, but have on both occasions failed.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> An agreement for the restoration of harmony between Chad and Sudan, signed 15 January 2010, marked the end of a five-year war.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The fix in relations led to the Chadian rebels from Sudan returning home, the opening of the border between the two countries after seven years of closure, and the deployment of a joint force to secure the border. In May 2013, security forces in Chad foiled a coup against the President <a href="/wiki/Idriss_Deby" title="Idriss Deby" class="mw-redirect">Idriss Deby</a> that had been in preparation for several months.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography.2C_climate_and_environment">Geography, climate and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography, climate and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Chad" title="Geography of Chad">Geography of Chad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chad_sat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Chad_sat.jpg/170px-Chad_sat.jpg" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Chad_sat.jpg/255px-Chad_sat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Chad_sat.jpg/340px-Chad_sat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1265" data-file-height="1922" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chad_sat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chad is divided into three distinct zones, the <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_savanna" title="Sudanese savanna" class="mw-redirect">Sudanese savanna</a> in the south, the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" title="Sahara Desert" class="mw-redirect">Sahara Desert</a> in the north, and the <a href="/wiki/Sahelian" title="Sahelian" class="mw-redirect">Sahelian</a> belt in Chad's center.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg/250px-ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg" width="250" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg/375px-ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg/500px-ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="566" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> in a 2001 satellite image. On the top, the changes from 1973 to 1997 are shown, with the lake shrinking.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 1,284,000 square kilometres (496,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), Chad is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area" class="mw-redirect">21st-largest country</a>. It is slightly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and slightly larger than South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Chad is in north central Africa, lying between latitudes <a href="/wiki/7th_parallel_north" title="7th parallel north">7°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_parallel_north" title="24th parallel north">24°N</a>, and <a href="/wiki/13th_meridian_east" title="13th meridian east">13°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_meridian_east" title="24th meridian east">24°E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chad is bounded to the north by <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, to the east by <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, to the west by <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, and to the south by the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>. The country's capital is 1,060 kilometres (660&#160;mi) from the nearest seaport, <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of this distance from the sea and the country's largely <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> climate, Chad is sometimes referred to as the "Dead Heart of Africa".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The dominant physical structure is a wide basin bounded to the north and east by the <a href="/wiki/Ennedi_Plateau" title="Ennedi Plateau">Ennedi Plateau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibesti_Mountains" title="Tibesti Mountains">Tibesti Mountains</a>, which include <a href="/wiki/Emi_Koussi" title="Emi Koussi">Emi Koussi</a>, a dormant volcano in that reaches 3,414 metres (11,201&#160;ft) above sea level. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>, after which the country is named, is the remains of an immense lake that occupied 330,000 square kilometres (130,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the <a href="/wiki/Chad_Basin" title="Chad Basin">Chad Basin</a> 7,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Although in the 21st century it covers only 17,806 square kilometres (6,875&#160;sq&#160;mi), and its surface area is subject to heavy seasonal fluctuations,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> the lake is Africa's second largest wetland.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The region's tall grasses and extensive marshes make it favourable for birds, reptiles, and large mammals. Chad's major rivers—the <a href="/wiki/Chari_River" title="Chari River">Chari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logone_River" title="Logone River">Logone</a> and their tributaries—flow through the southern savannas from the southeast into Lake Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Chad" title="Climate of Chad" class="mw-redirect">Climate of Chad</a></div>
<p>Each year a tropical weather system known as the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">intertropical front</a> crosses Chad from south to north, bringing a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> that lasts from May to October in the south, and from June to September in the Sahel.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Variations in local rainfall create three major geographical zones. The Sahara lies in the country's northern third. Yearly precipitations throughout this belt are under 50 millimetres (2.0&#160;in); only the occasional spontaneous palm grove survives, and the only ones to do so are south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Sahara gives way to a <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a> belt in Chad's centre; precipitation there varies from 300 to 600&#160;mm (11.8 to 23.6&#160;in) per year. In the Sahel, a steppe of thorny bushes (mostly <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacias</a>) gradually gives way to the south to <a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna" class="mw-redirect">East Sudanian savanna</a> in Chad's <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudanese</a> zone. Yearly rainfall in this belt is over 900&#160;mm (35.4&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Chad" title="Wildlife of Chad">Wildlife of Chad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg/220px-African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg/330px-African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg/440px-African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1044" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/African_bush_elephant" title="African bush elephant">African bush elephant</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chad's animal and plant life correspond to the three climatic zones. In the Saharan region, the only flora is the date-palm groves of the oasis. Palms and <a href="/wiki/Acacia_tree" title="Acacia tree" class="mw-redirect">acacia trees</a> grow in the Sahelian region. The southern, or Sudanic, zone consists of broad grasslands or prairies suitable for grazing. As of 2002, there were at least 134 species of mammals, 509 species of birds (354 species of residents and 155 migrants), and over 1,600 species of plants throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Flora_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flora-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">Elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Buffalo" title="African Buffalo" class="mw-redirect">buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">hippopotamuses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceroses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giraffe" title="Giraffe">giraffes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheetah" title="Cheetah">cheetahs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyenas" title="Hyenas" class="mw-redirect">hyenas</a>, and many species of <a href="/wiki/Snakes" title="Snakes" class="mw-redirect">snakes</a> are found here, although most large carnivore populations have been drastically reduced since the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LTQ_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LTQ-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elephant_hunting_in_Chad" title="Elephant hunting in Chad">Elephant poaching</a>, particularly in the south of the country in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Zakouma_National_Park" title="Zakouma National Park">Zakouma National Park</a>, is a severe problem.</p>
<p>Extensive deforestation has resulted in loss of trees such as acacias, baobab, dates and palm trees. This has also caused loss of natural habitat for wild animals; one of the main reasons for this is also hunting and livestock farming by increasing human settlements. Animals like lions, leopards and rhino have been almost decimated.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Efforts have been made by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agricultural_Organization" title="Food and Agricultural Organization" class="mw-redirect">Food and Agricultural Organization</a> to improve relations between farmers, agro-pastoralists and pastoralists in the Zakouma National Park (ZNP), Siniaka-Minia, and Aouk reserve in southeastern Chad to promote sustainable development.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> As part of the national conservation effort, more than 1.2 million trees have been replanted to check the advancement of the desert, which incidentally also helps the local economy by way of financial return from acacia trees, which produce <a href="/wiki/Gum_arabic" title="Gum arabic">gum arabic</a>, and also from fruit trees.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Poaching is a serious problem in the country, particularly of elephants for the profitable <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a> industry and a threat to lives of rangers even in the national parks such as Zakouma. Elephants are often massacred in herds in and around the parks by organized poaching.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The problem is worsened by the fact that the parks are understaffed and that a number of wardens have been murdered by poachers.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Chad" title="Demographics of Chad">Demographics of Chad</a></div>
<p>2005 estimates place Chad's population at 10,146,000; 25.8% live in urban areas and 74.8% in rural ones.<sup id="cite_ref-PopulationProspects_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopulationProspects-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The country's population is young: an estimated 47.3% is under 15. The birth rate is estimated at 42.35 births per 1,000 people, the mortality rate at 16.69. The life expectancy is 47.2 years.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:180px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ouaddaian_girl_from_Chad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Ouaddaian_girl_from_Chad.jpg" width="178" height="197" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="178" data-file-height="197" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ouaddaian_girl_from_Chad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Ouadda%C3%AF_Region" title="Ouaddaï Region">Ouaddaian</a> girl</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chad's population is unevenly distributed. Density is 0.1/km<sup>2</sup> (0.26/sq&#160;mi) in the Saharan <a href="/wiki/Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti_Region" title="Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region">Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region</a> but 52.4/km<sup>2</sup> (136/sq&#160;mi) in the <a href="/wiki/Logone_Occidental_Region" title="Logone Occidental Region">Logone Occidental Region</a>. In the capital, it is even higher.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> About half of the nation's population lives in the southern fifth of its territory, making this the most densely populated region.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Urban life is virtually restricted to the capital, whose population is mostly engaged in commerce. The other major towns are <a href="/wiki/Sarh" title="Sarh">Sarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moundou" title="Moundou">Moundou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ab%C3%A9ch%C3%A9" title="Abéché">Abéché</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doba" title="Doba">Doba</a>, which are less urbanised but are growing rapidly and joining the capital as decisive factors in economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2003, 230,000 <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_refugees_in_Chad" title="Sudanese refugees in Chad">Sudanese refugees</a> have fled to eastern Chad from war-ridden Darfur. With the 172,600 Chadians displaced by the civil war in the east, this has generated increased tensions among the region's communities.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">Polygamy</a> is common, with 39% of women living in such unions. This is sanctioned by law, which automatically permits polygamy unless spouses specify that this is unacceptable upon marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Although violence against women is prohibited, domestic violence is common. <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_cutting" title="Female genital cutting" class="mw-redirect">Female genital mutilation</a> is also prohibited, but the practice is widespread and deeply rooted in tradition; 45% of Chadian women undergo the procedure, with the highest rates among <a href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab" class="mw-redirect">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hadjarai" title="Hadjarai" class="mw-redirect">Hadjarai</a>, and Ouaddaians (90% or more). Lower percentages were reported among the <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a> (38%) and the <a href="/wiki/Toubou" title="Toubou" class="mw-redirect">Toubou</a> (2%). Women lack equal opportunities in education and training, making it difficult for them to compete for the relatively few formal-sector jobs. Although property and inheritance laws based on the French code do not discriminate against women, local leaders adjudicate most inheritance cases in favour of men, according to traditional practice.<sup id="cite_ref-HRP_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRP-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups_in_Chad">Ethnic groups in Chad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups in Chad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Chad" title="Ethnic groups in Chad">Ethnic groups in Chad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_delegation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Chadian_delegation.jpg/250px-Chadian_delegation.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Chadian_delegation.jpg/375px-Chadian_delegation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Chadian_delegation.jpg/500px-Chadian_delegation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_delegation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A tribal delegation</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chad has more than 200 distinct ethnic groups,<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> which create diverse social structures. The colonial administration and independent governments have attempted to impose a national society, but for most Chadians the local or regional society remains the most important influence outside the immediate family. Nevertheless, Chad's peoples may be classified according to the geographical region in which they live.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the south live sedentary people such as the <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a>, the nation's main ethnic group, whose essential <a href="/wiki/Social_unit" title="Social unit" class="mw-redirect">social unit</a> is the lineage. In the Sahel sedentary peoples live side-by-side with nomadic ones, such as the Arabs, the country's second major ethnic group. The north is inhabited by nomads, mostly Toubous.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Chad" title="Languages of Chad">Languages of Chad</a></div>
<p>Chad's official business languages are <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, but over 100 languages and dialects are spoken. Due to the important role played by itinerant Arab traders and settled merchants in local communities, <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Arabic" title="Chadian Arabic">Chadian Arabic</a> has become a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Chad" title="Religion in Chad">Religion in Chad</a></div>
<p>Chad is a religiously diverse country. The 1993 census found that 54% of Chadians were <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Chad" title="Islam in Chad">Muslim</a> (of these, according to a Pew report 48% professed to be <a href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni" class="mw-redirect">Sunni</a>, 21% <a href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia" class="mw-redirect">Shia</a>, 4% <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadi</a> and 23% <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim" class="mw-redirect">just Muslim</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-pew128_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew128-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Of the others, 20% were <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Chad" title="Roman Catholicism in Chad">Roman Catholic</a>, 14% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>, 10% <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animist</a>, while 3% didn't profess any religion.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> None of these religious traditions are monolithic. Animism includes a variety of ancestor and place-oriented religions whose expression is highly specific. Islam is expressed in diverse ways; for example, according to the Pew report mentioned earlier 55% of Muslim Chadians belong to <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> <a href="/wiki/Tariqa" title="Tariqa">orders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pew128_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew128-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Africa" title="Christianity in Africa">Christianity</a> arrived in Chad with the French and American missionaries; as with Chadian Islam, it <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretises</a> aspects of pre-Christian religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Muslims are largely concentrated in northern and eastern Chad, and animists and Christians live primarily in southern Chad and <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A9ra_Region" title="Guéra Region">Guéra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The constitution provides for a secular state and guarantees religious freedom; different religious communities generally co-exist without problems.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Chad" title="Freedom of religion in Chad">Other</a></td>

</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>The majority of Muslims in the country are adherents of a moderate branch of mystical Islam (<a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>). Its most common expression is the <a href="/wiki/Tijaniyah" title="Tijaniyah" class="mw-redirect">Tijaniyah</a>, an order followed by the 35% of Chadian Muslims which incorporates some local African religious elements.<sup id="cite_ref-pew128_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew128-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> A small minority of the country's Muslims hold more fundamentalist practices, which, in some cases, may be associated with Saudi-oriented <a href="/wiki/Salafi_movement" title="Salafi movement">Salafi movements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Roman Catholics represent the largest Christian denomination in the country. Most Protestants, including the Nigeria-based "Winners Chapel", are affiliated with various evangelical Christian groups. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" title="Bahá'í" class="mw-redirect">Bahá'í</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> religious communities also are present in the country. Both faiths were introduced after independence in 1960 and therefore are considered to be "new" religions in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chad is home to foreign missionaries representing both Christian and Islamic groups. Itinerant Muslim preachers, primarily from Sudan, Saudi Arabia, and Pakistan, also visit. Saudi Arabian funding generally supports social and educational projects and extensive mosque construction.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Chad" title="Politics of Chad">Politics of Chad</a></div>
<p>Chad's constitution provides for a strong executive branch headed by a president who dominates the political system. The president has the power to appoint the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Chad" title="Prime Minister of Chad" class="mw-redirect">prime minister</a> and the cabinet, and exercises considerable influence over appointments of judges, generals, provincial officials and heads of Chad's para-statal firms. In cases of grave and immediate threat, the president, in consultation with the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Chad)" title="National Assembly (Chad)">National Assembly</a>, may declare a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>. The president is <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Chad" title="Elections in Chad">directly elected</a> by popular vote for a five-year term; in 2005 constitutional term limits were removed,<sup id="cite_ref-Term2_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Term2-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> allowing a president to remain in power beyond the previous two-term limit.<sup id="cite_ref-Term2_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Term2-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of Déby's key advisers are members of the Zaghawa ethnic group, although southern and opposition personalities are represented in <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Chad" title="Government of Chad">government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNPACP_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPACP-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chad's legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_France" title="Law of France">French civil law</a> and Chadian customary law where the latter does not interfere with public order or constitutional guarantees of equality. Despite the constitution's guarantee of judicial independence, the president names most key judicial officials. The legal system's highest jurisdictions, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Chad" title="Supreme Court of Chad">Supreme Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Council_of_Chad" title="Constitutional Council of Chad">Constitutional Council</a>, have become fully operational since 2000. The Supreme Court is made up of a chief justice, named by the president, and 15 councillors, appointed for life by the president and the National Assembly. The Constitutional Court is headed by nine judges elected to nine-year terms. It has the power to review legislation, treaties and international agreements prior to their adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNPACP_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPACP-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Chad_(Washington,_D.C.).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG/220px-Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG/330px-Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG/440px-Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1976" data-file-height="1712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Chad_(Washington,_D.C.).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Chad_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of Chad in Washington, D.C.">Embassy of Chad in Washington, D.C.</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The National Assembly makes legislation. The body consists of 155 members elected for four-year terms who meet three times per year. The Assembly holds regular sessions twice a year, starting in March and October, and can hold special sessions when called by the prime minister. Deputies elect a National Assembly president every two years. The president must sign or reject newly passed laws within 15 days. The National Assembly must approve the prime minister's plan of government and may force the prime minister to resign through a majority vote of no confidence. However, if the National Assembly rejects the executive branch's programme twice in one year, the president may disband the Assembly and call for new legislative elections. In practice, the president exercises considerable influence over the National Assembly through his party, the <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_Salvation_Movement" title="Patriotic Salvation Movement">Patriotic Salvation Movement</a> (MPS), which holds a large majority.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_parties">Political parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Chad" title="List of political parties in Chad">List of political parties in Chad</a></div>
<p>Until the legalisation of opposition parties in 1992, Déby's MPS was the sole legal party in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Since then, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Chad" title="List of political parties in Chad">78 registered political parties</a> have become active.<sup id="cite_ref-HRP_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRP-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, opposition parties and human rights organisations supported the boycott of the constitutional referendum that allowed Déby to stand for re-election for a third term<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> amid reports of widespread irregularities in voter registration and government censorship of independent media outlets during the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Correspondents judged the 2006 presidential elections a mere formality, as the opposition deemed the polls a farce and boycotted them.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_opposition_and_foreign_relations">Internal opposition and foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Internal opposition and foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Chad" title="Foreign relations of Chad">Foreign relations of Chad</a></div>
<p>Déby faces armed opposition from groups who are deeply divided by leadership clashes but united in their intention to overthrow him.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> These forces <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2006)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2006)">stormed the capital</a> on 13 April 2006, but were ultimately repelled. Chad's greatest foreign influence is France, which maintains 1,000 soldiers in the country. Déby relies on the French to help repel the rebels, and France gives the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Chad" title="Military of Chad">Chadian army</a> logistical and intelligence support for fear of a complete collapse of regional stability.<sup id="cite_ref-PINR_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PINR-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, Franco-Chadian relations were soured by the granting of oil drilling rights to the American <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">Exxon</a> company in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chad is listed as a failed state by the <a href="/wiki/Fund_for_Peace" title="Fund for Peace">Fund for Peace</a> (FFP). In 2007 Chad had the seventh highest score on the failed state index. Since then the trend has been upwards each year. Chad had the fourth highest score (behind Sudan) on the Failed State Index of 2012 and as of 2013, is ranked fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-fundforpeace.org_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fundforpeace.org-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Corruption is rife at all levels; <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> for 2005 named Chad (tied with <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>) as the most corrupt country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Chad's ranking on the index has improved only marginally in recent years. Since its first inclusion on the index in 2004, Chad's best score has been 2/10 for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics of President Déby have accused him of cronyism and tribalism.<sup id="cite_ref-tribe_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tribe-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> <sup style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Punctuation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style"><span title="Quotation marks may be incomplete, unbalanced or improperly applied.">check quotation syntax</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Chad" title="Regions of Chad">Regions of Chad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Chad" title="Departments of Chad">Departments of Chad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-prefectures_of_Chad" title="Sub-prefectures of Chad">Sub-prefectures of Chad</a></div>
<p>Chad has been divided since February 2008 into <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Chad" title="Regions of Chad">22 regions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-circonscritions_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circonscritions-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The subdivision of Chad in regions came about in 2003 as part of the decentralisation process, when the government abolished the previous <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Chad" title="Prefectures of Chad">14 prefectures</a>. Each region is headed by a presidentially appointed governor. Prefects administer the <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Chad" title="Departments of Chad">61 departments</a> within the regions.<sup id="cite_ref-circonscritions_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circonscritions-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The departments are divided into <a href="/wiki/Sub-prefectures_of_Chad" title="Sub-prefectures of Chad">200 sub-prefectures</a>, which are in turn composed of 446 cantons.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The cantons are scheduled to be replaced by <i>communautés rurales</i>, but the legal and regulatory framework has not yet been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-WB1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB1-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The constitution provides for decentralised government to compel local populations to play an active role in their own development.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> To this end, the constitution declares that each administrative subdivisions be governed by elected local assemblies,<sup id="cite_ref-decentralisation_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decentralisation-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> but no local elections have taken place,<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> and communal elections scheduled for 2005 have been repeatedly postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-HRP_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRP-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The regions are:<sup id="cite_ref-circonscritions_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circonscritions-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
