<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Chad" title="Military of Chad">Military of Chad</a></div>
<p>As of 2011, Chad currently spends 1.6% of GDP on its army, a drastic drop from the level of 2009 (4.2% of GDP), when the country was engaged in a <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Civil_War_(2005%E2%80%932010)" title="Chadian Civil War (2005–2010)" class="mw-redirect">civil war</a>, with rebels supported by neighboring <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> This then increased to 2.0% of GDP in 2013, when Chad began its <a href="/wiki/FATIM" title="FATIM" class="mw-redirect">military intervention</a> in Northern Mali, to help France and other African nations in bringing back Mali's sovereignty over the North. The army has over 30,350 active personnel and 3,000,000 fit for military service, making it the most efficient force in the region besides the army of <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebel_groups">Rebel groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Rebel groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Rebel_groups_in_Chad" title="Category:Rebel groups in Chad">Category:Rebel groups in Chad</a></div>
<p>There have been numerous rebel groups in Chad throughout the last few decades. In 2007, a peace treaty was signed that integrated <a href="/wiki/United_Front_for_Democratic_Change" title="United Front for Democratic Change">United Front for Democratic Change</a> or <b>FUC</b> soldiers into the Chadian Army.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Justice_and_Democracy_in_Chad" title="Movement for Justice and Democracy in Chad" class="mw-redirect">Movement for Justice and Democracy in Chad</a> or <b>MDJT</b> also clashed with government forces in 2003 in an attempt to overthrow President <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a>. In addition, there have been various conflicts with <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a> rebels in Eastern Chad who killed civilians by use of <a href="/wiki/Helicopter_gunship" title="Helicopter gunship" class="mw-redirect">helicopter gunships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Presently, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Resistance_Forces" title="Union of Resistance Forces">Union of Resistance Forces</a> or <b>UFR</b> are a rebel group that continues to battle with the government of Chad. In 2010, the UFR reportedly had a force estimating 6,000 men and 300 vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Chad" title="Law enforcement in Chad">Law enforcement in Chad</a></div>
<p>In Chad, the Gendarmerie Nationale serves as the national police force for the country.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Chad" title="Economy of Chad">Economy of Chad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Chad" title="Agriculture in Chad">Agriculture in Chad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="865" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graphical depiction of Chad's product exports in 28 color-coded categories.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> ranks Chad as the seventh poorest country in the world, with 80% of the population living below the poverty line. The <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">Purchasing power parity</a>) per capita was estimated as <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1,651 in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Chad is part of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Central_African_States" title="Bank of Central African States">Bank of Central African States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Customs_and_Economic_Union_of_Central_Africa" title="Customs and Economic Union of Central Africa" class="mw-redirect">Customs and Economic Union of Central Africa</a> (UDEAC) and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa" class="mw-redirect">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chad's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_CFA_franc" title="Central African CFA franc">CFA franc</a>. In the 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Chad" title="Mining industry of Chad">Mining industry of Chad</a> produced <a href="/wiki/Sodium_carbonate" title="Sodium carbonate">sodium carbonate</a>, or natron. There have also been reports of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>-bearing quartz in the <a href="/wiki/Biltine_Prefecture" title="Biltine Prefecture">Biltine Prefecture</a>. However, years of civil war have scared away foreign investors; those who left Chad between 1979 and 1982 have only recently begun to regain confidence in the country's future. In 2000 major direct foreign investment in the oil sector began, boosting the country's economic prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_Women.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mao_Women.jpg/250px-Mao_Women.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mao_Women.jpg/375px-Mao_Women.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0f/Mao_Women.jpg 2x" data-file-width="477" data-file-height="318" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_Women.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Women in <a href="/wiki/Mao,_Chad" title="Mao, Chad">Mao</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Utilities_in_Chad" title="Utilities in Chad">water</a> is provided by a water tower. Access to clean water is often a problem in Chad.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over 80% of Chad's population relies on subsistence farming and livestock raising for its livelihood.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The crops grown and the locations of herds are determined by the local climate. In the southernmost 10% of the territory lies the nation's most fertile cropland, with rich yields of <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>. In the Sahel only the hardier varieties of millet grow, and these with much lower yields than in the south. On the other hand, the Sahel is ideal pastureland for large herds of commercial cattle and for goats, sheep, donkeys and horses. The Sahara's scattered <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oases</a> support only some dates and legumes.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Chad's cities face serious difficulties of municipal infrastructure; only 48% of urban residents have access to potable water and only 2% to basic sanitation.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WB1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB1-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Before the development of oil industry, cotton dominated industry and the labour market had accounted for approximately 80% of export earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Cotton remains a primary export, although exact figures are not available. Rehabilitation of <a href="/wiki/Cotontchad" title="Cotontchad">Cotontchad</a>, a major cotton company that suffered from a decline in world cotton prices, has been financed by France, the Netherlands, the European Union, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> (IBRD). The <a href="/wiki/Parastatal" title="Parastatal" class="mw-redirect">parastatal</a> is now expected to be privatised.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>If Chad can maintain a semblance of stability foreign investments will eventually return, but even 24 years after the last successful coup that brought President Idris Deby to power, investors are still wary of investing in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_situation">Humanitarian situation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Humanitarian situation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Chad" title="Human rights in Chad">Human rights in Chad</a></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, Chad has been affected by a <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_crisis" title="Humanitarian crisis">humanitarian crisis</a> since at least 2001. As of 2008, the country of Chad hosts over 280,000 refugees from the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> region, over 55,000 from the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, as well as over 170,000 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2008 in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2008)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2008)">battle of N'Djamena</a>, UN Under-Secretary-General for Humanitarian Affairs <a href="/wiki/John_Holmes_(British_diplomat)" title="John Holmes (British diplomat)">John Holmes</a> expressed "extreme concern" that the crisis would have a negative effect on the ability of humanitarians to deliver life-saving assistance to half a million beneficiaries, most of whom – according to him – heavily rely on humanitarian aid for their survival.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> UN spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Giuliano" title="Maurizio Giuliano">Maurizio Giuliano</a> stated to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>: "If we do not manage to provide aid at sufficient levels, the humanitarian crisis might become a humanitarian catastrophe".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> have suspended activities due to killings of aid workers.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Chad" title="Transport in Chad">Transport in Chad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg/250px-Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg/375px-Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg/500px-Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A bridge on the <a href="/wiki/Bragoto_River" title="Bragoto River">Bragoto River</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Civil war crippled the development of <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Chad" title="Transport in Chad">transport infrastructure</a>; in 1987, Chad had only 30 kilometres (19&#160;mi) of paved roads. Successive road rehabilitation projects improved the network<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> to 550 kilometres (340&#160;mi) by 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, the road network is limited; roads are often unusable for several months of the year. With no railways of its own, Chad depends heavily on Cameroon's rail system for the transport of Chadian exports and imports to and from the seaport of <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Chad" title="List of airports in Chad">List of airports in Chad</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg/250px-Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg/375px-Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg/500px-Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="453" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An airplane landing in <a href="/wiki/Ab%C3%A9ch%C3%A9" title="Abéché">Abéché</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena_International_Airport" title="N'Djamena International Airport">international airport</a> serves the capital and provides regular nonstop flights to Paris and several African cities.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Chad" title="Rail transport in Chad">Rail transport in Chad</a></div>
<p>At the beginning of the 20th century, a railway system was in development near Lake Chad. In the 21st century, Chad and the <a href="/wiki/China_Civil_Engineering_Construction" title="China Civil Engineering Construction">China Civil Engineering Construction Corp</a> agreed to a $7 billion contract to build additional railway infrastructure. Presently, there are rail links to Libya and Sudan.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Chad" title="Energy in Chad">Energy in Chad</a></div>
<p>Chad's energy sector has suffered from years of mismanagement by the parastatal Chad Water and Electric Society (STEE), which provides power for 15% of the capital's citizens and covers only 1.5% of the national population.<sup id="cite_ref-CCG_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Most Chadians burn biomass fuels such as wood and animal manure for power.<sup id="cite_ref-EIA_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a> leads a consortium of <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petronas" title="Petronas">Petronas</a> that has invested $3.7 billion to develop oil reserves estimated at one billion barrels in southern Chad. Oil production began in 2003 with the <a href="/wiki/Chad-Cameroon_Petroleum_Development_and_Pipeline_Project" title="Chad-Cameroon Petroleum Development and Pipeline Project" class="mw-redirect">completion of a pipeline</a> (financed in part by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>) that links the southern oilfields to terminals on the Atlantic coast of Cameroon. As a condition of its assistance, the World Bank insisted that 80% of oil revenues be spent on development projects. In January 2006 the World Bank suspended its loan programme when the Chadian government passed laws reducing this amount.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OECD_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> On 14 July 2006, the World Bank and Chad signed a memorandum of understanding under which the Government of Chad commits 70% of its spending to priority poverty reduction programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Chad" title="Telecommunications in Chad">Telecommunications in Chad</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Chad" title="Communications in Chad" class="mw-redirect">telecommunication system</a> is basic and expensive, with fixed telephone services provided by the state telephone company <a href="/wiki/SotelTchad" title="SotelTchad">SotelTchad</a>. Only 14,000 fixed telephone lines serve all of Chad, one of the lowest telephone density rates in the world.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gateway_Communications" title="Gateway Communications">Gateway Communications</a>, a pan-African wholesale connectivity and telecommunications provider also has a presence in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2013, Chad's Ministry for Posts and Information &amp; Communication Technologies (PNTIC) announced that the country will be seeking a partner for <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">fiber optic</a> technology.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_phones">Mobile phones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mobile phones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In September 2010 the penetration rate was estimated at 24.3% over a population estimate of 10.7 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Chad_Mobile_Market_.28Q1_2008_-_Q3_2010.29_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chad_Mobile_Market_.28Q1_2008_-_Q3_2010.29-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chad is ranked last in the World Economic Forum's Network Readiness Index (NRI) – an indicator for determining the development level of a country’s information and communication technologies. Chad ranked number 148 out of 148 overall in the 2014 NRI ranking, down from 142 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Chad" title="Media of Chad">Media of Chad</a></div>
<p>Chad's television audience is limited to N'Djamena. The only television station is the state-owned TeleTchad. Radio has a far greater reach, with 13 private radio stations.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Newspapers are limited in quantity and distribution, and circulation figures are small due to transportation costs, low literacy rates, and poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EIA_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> While the constitution defends liberty of expression, the government has regularly restricted this right, and at the end of 2006 began to enact a system of prior <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> on the media.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Chad" title="Education in Chad">Educators</a> face considerable challenges due to the nation's dispersed population and a certain degree of reluctance on the part of parents to send their children to school. Although attendance is compulsory, only 68 percent of boys attend primary school, and more than half of the population is illiterate. <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Chad" title="List of universities in Chad">Higher education</a> is provided at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_N%27Djamena" title="University of N'Djamena">University of N'Djamena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BGN_52-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> At 33 percent, Chad has one of the lowest literacy rates of Sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><br />
In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" title="U.S. Department of Labor" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Department of Labor</a>'s Findings on the Worst Forms of Child Labor<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> in Chad reported that school attendance of children aged 5 to 14 was as low as 39%. This can also be related to the issue of <a href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor" class="mw-redirect">child labor</a> as the report also stated that 53% of children aged 5 to 14 were working children, and that 30% of children aged 7 to 14 combined work and school. A more recent DOL <a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">report</a> listed cattle herding as a major agricultural activity that employed underage children.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin:10px;">
<caption><b>Holidays</b><sup id="cite_ref-CCG_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></caption>
<tr>
<th style="font-size: smaller;">Date</th>
<th style="font-size: smaller;">English Name</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1 January</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1 May</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a></td>
</tr>

</tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>1 November</td>

<td><a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Because of its great variety of peoples and languages, Chad possesses a rich cultural heritage. The Chadian government has actively promoted Chadian culture and national traditions by opening the <a href="/wiki/Chad_National_Museum" title="Chad National Museum">Chad National Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chad_Cultural_Centre" title="Chad Cultural Centre">Chad Cultural Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_32-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Six <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Chad" title="Public holidays in Chad">national holidays</a> are observed throughout the year, and movable holidays include the Christian holiday of <a href="/wiki/Easter_Monday" title="Easter Monday">Easter Monday</a> and the Muslim holidays of <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" title="Eid ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect">Eid ul-Fitr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Adha" title="Eid ul-Adha" class="mw-redirect">Eid ul-Adha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Eid Milad Nnabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CCG_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Chad" title="Music of Chad">music of Chad</a> includes a number of unusual instruments such as the <i>kinde</i>, a type of bow harp; the <i><a href="/wiki/Kakaki" title="Kakaki">kakaki</a></i>, a long tin horn; and the <i>hu hu</i>, a stringed instrument that uses <a href="/wiki/Calabash" title="Calabash">calabashes</a> as loudspeakers. Other instruments and their combinations are more linked to specific ethnic groups: the Sara prefer whistles, <a href="/wiki/Balafon" title="Balafon">balafones</a>, harps and <i>kodjo</i> drums; and the <a href="/wiki/Kanembu_people" title="Kanembu people">Kanembu</a> combine the sounds of drums with those of flute-like instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tailor_in_Chad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Tailor_in_Chad.jpg/250px-Tailor_in_Chad.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Tailor_in_Chad.jpg/375px-Tailor_in_Chad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Tailor_in_Chad.jpg/500px-Tailor_in_Chad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tailor_in_Chad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Chadian tailor sells traditional dresses.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The music group <a href="/wiki/Chari_Jazz" title="Chari Jazz">Chari Jazz</a> formed in 1964 and initiated Chad's modern music scene. Later, more renowned groups such as African Melody and International Challal attempted to mix modernity and tradition. Popular groups such as Tibesti have clung faster to their heritage by drawing on <i>sai</i>, a traditional style of music from southern Chad. The people of Chad have customarily disdained modern music. However, in 1995 greater interest has developed and fostered the distribution of CDs and audio cassettes featuring Chadian artists. Piracy and a lack of legal protections for artists' rights remain problems to further development of the Chadian music industry.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chadian_cuisine" title="Chadian cuisine">Chadian cuisine</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">Millet</a> is the staple food throughout Chad. It is used to make balls of paste that are dipped in sauces. In the north this dish is known as <i>alysh</i>; in the south, as <i>biya</i>. Fish is popular, which is generally prepared and sold either as <i>salanga</i> (sun-dried and lightly smoked <i><a href="/wiki/Alestes" title="Alestes">Alestes</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hydrocynus" title="Hydrocynus">Hydrocynus</a></i>) or as <i>banda</i> (smoked large fish).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Carcaje</i> is a popular sweet red tea extracted from hibiscus leaves. Alcoholic beverages, though absent in the north, are popular in the south, where people drink <a href="/wiki/Millet_beer" title="Millet beer">millet beer</a>, known as <i>billi-billi</i> when brewed from red millet, and as <i>coshate</i> when from <a href="/wiki/Proso_millet" title="Proso millet">white millet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chadian_literature" title="Chadian literature">Chadian literature</a></div>
<p>As in other Sahelian countries, literature in Chad has suffered from an economic, political and spiritual drought that has affected its best known writers. Chadian authors have been forced to write from exile or expatriate status and have generated literature dominated by themes of political oppression and historical discourse. Since 1962, 20 Chadian authors have written some 60 works of fiction. Among the most internationally renowned writers are <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Brahim_Se%C3%AFd" title="Joseph Brahim Seïd" class="mw-redirect">Joseph Brahim Seïd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baba_Moustapha" title="Baba Moustapha">Baba Moustapha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Bangui" title="Antoine Bangui">Antoine Bangui</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koulsy_Lamko" title="Koulsy Lamko">Koulsy Lamko</a>. In 2003 Chad's sole literary critic, <a href="/wiki/Ahmat_Taboye" title="Ahmat Taboye">Ahmat Taboye</a>, published his <span lang="fr"><i>Anthologie de la littérature tchadienne</i></span> to further knowledge of Chad's literature internationally and among youth and to make up for Chad's lack of publishing houses and promotional structure.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The development of a Chadian film industry has suffered from the devastations of civil war and from the lack of <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">cinemas</a>, of which there is only one in the whole country. The first Chadian <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">feature film</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Docudrama" title="Docudrama">docudrama</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Bye_Bye_Africa" title="Bye Bye Africa">Bye Bye Africa</a></i>, was made in 1999 by <a href="/wiki/Mahamat_Saleh_Haroun" title="Mahamat Saleh Haroun">Mahamat Saleh Haroun</a>. His later film <i><a href="/wiki/Abouna" title="Abouna">Abouna</a></i> was critically acclaimed, and his <i><a href="/wiki/Daratt" title="Daratt">Daratt</a></i> won the Grand Special Jury Prize at the <a href="/wiki/63rd_Venice_International_Film_Festival" title="63rd Venice International Film Festival">63rd Venice International Film Festival</a>. The 2010 feature film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Screaming_Man" title="A Screaming Man">A Screaming Man</a></i> won the <a href="/wiki/Jury_Prize_(Cannes_Film_Festival)" title="Jury Prize (Cannes Film Festival)">Jury Prize</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2010 Cannes Film Festival">2010 Cannes Film Festival</a>, making Haroun the first Chadian director to enter, as well as win, an award in the main Cannes competition.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Issa_Serge_Coelo" title="Issa Serge Coelo">Issa Serge Coelo</a> directed Chad's two other films, <i><a href="/wiki/Daresalam" title="Daresalam">Daresalam</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/DP75:_Tartina_City" title="DP75: Tartina City">DP75: Tartina City</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Chad" title="Sport in Chad">Sport in Chad</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is Chad's most popular <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Chad" title="Sport in Chad">sport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Chad_national_football_team" title="Chad national football team">national team</a> is closely followed during international competitions<sup id="cite_ref-culture_105-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> and Chadian footballers have played for French teams. <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling" title="Freestyle wrestling">freestyle wrestling</a> are widely practiced, the latter in a form in which the wrestlers put on traditional animal hides and cover themselves with dust.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_105-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
